        <div id="readme" class="Box-body readme blob js-code-block-container p-5 p-xl-6 gist-border-0">
    <article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-overview" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Overview</h2>
<p dir="auto">These are a list of useful commands from <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Loav1kbA640" rel="nofollow">this</a> video on Youtube by Siraj Raval.</p>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-useful-git-commands" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#useful-git-commands"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Useful Git Commands</h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-about-it" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#about-it"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>About it</h2>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Have you recently started using Git? This should give you the base commands you need to perform the most common actions in Git. If you find a command that is not here, or could be explained better, please don't hesitate in * <a href="#contributing">Contributing</a>. Cheers!</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-table-of-contents" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#table-of-contents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Table of contents</h2>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="#install-git">Install git</a></li>
<li><a href="#setting-up-git">Setting up git</a></li>

<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-git" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#git"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Git</h4>
<p dir="auto">Git is a distributed version control system, very easy to learn and supper fast!</p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-install-git" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#install-git"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Install Git</h4>
<p dir="auto">There are a few different ways to install git (from source or for Linux) but the purpose of this page is to focus on git commands, so I am going to assume you are installing git on a Mac.</p>
<p dir="auto">To view other ways of installing it visit the <a href="http://git-scm.com/book/en/Getting-Started-Installing-Git" rel="nofollow">Git official site</a></p>
<p dir="auto">Click <a href="http://git-scm.com/download/mac" rel="nofollow">here</a> to download and install Git</p>
<h5 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-setting-up-git" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#setting-up-git"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Setting up git</h5>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git config --global user.name &quot;User Name&quot;

$ git config --global user.email &quot;email&quot;"><pre>$ git config --global user.name <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>User Name<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

$ git config --global user.email <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>email<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<h5 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-applying-colour-to-git" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#applying-colour-to-git"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Applying colour to git</h5>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git config --global color.ui true"><pre>$ git config --global color.ui <span class="pl-c1">true</span></pre></div>
<h5 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-initializing-a-repository-in-an-existing-directory" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#initializing-a-repository-in-an-existing-directory"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Initializing a repository in an existing directory</h5>
<p dir="auto">If you’re starting to track an existing project in Git, you need to go to the project’s directory and type:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git init"><pre>$ git init</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This creates a new subdirectory named .git that contains all of your necessary repository files — a Git repository skeleton. At this point, nothing in your project is tracked yet.</p>
<p dir="auto">To start version-controlling existing files you should start by tracking those files and do an initial commit. To accomplish that you should start with a few  <code>$ git add</code> that specifies the files you want to track followed by a commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git add &lt;file&gt;
$ git add README
$ git commit -m 'Initial project version'"><pre>$ git add <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>file<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
$ git add README
$ git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Initial project version<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span></pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-checking-the-status-of-your-files" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#checking-the-status-of-your-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Checking the status of your files</h4>
<p dir="auto">The main tool you use to determine which files are in which state is the <code>$ git status</code> command. If you run this command directly after a clone, you should see something like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git status
# On branch master
nothing to commit (working directory clean)"><pre>$ git status
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> On branch master</span>
nothing to commit (working directory clean)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">If you add a new file to your project, and the file didn't exist before, when you run a <code>$ git status</code> you should see your untracked file like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git status
# On branch master
# Untracked files:
#   (use &quot;git add &lt;file&gt;...&quot; to include in what will be committed)
#
#   README
nothing added to commit but untracked files present (use &quot;git add&quot; to track)"><pre>$ git status
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> On branch master</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Untracked files:</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>   (use "git add &lt;file&gt;..." to include in what will be committed)</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span></span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>   README</span>
nothing added to commit but untracked files present (use <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>git add<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> to track)</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-staging-files" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#staging-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Staging files</h4>
<p dir="auto">After initializing a git repository in the chosen directory, all files will now be tracked. Any changes made to any file will be shown after a <code>$ git status</code> as changes not staged for commit.</p>
<p dir="auto">To stage changes for commit you need to add the file(s) - or in other words, stage file(s).</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Adding a file
$ git add filename

# Adding all files
$ git add -A

# Adding all files changes in a directory
$ git add .

# Choosing what changes to add (this will got through all your changes and you can 'Y' or 'N' the changes)
$ git add -p"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Adding a file</span>
$ git add filename

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Adding all files</span>
$ git add -A

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Adding all files changes in a directory</span>
$ git add <span class="pl-c1">.</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Choosing what changes to add (this will got through all your changes and you can 'Y' or 'N' the changes)</span>
$ git add -p</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-stashing-files" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#stashing-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Stashing files</h4>
<p dir="auto">Git stash is a very useful command, where git will 'hide' the changes on a dirty directory - but no worries you can re-apply them later. The command will save your local changes away and revert the working directory to match the HEAD commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Stash local changes
$ git stash

# Stash local changes with a custom message
$ git stash save &quot;this is your custom message&quot;

# Re-apply the changes you saved in your latest stash
$ git stash apply

# Re-apply the changes you saved in a given stash number
$ git stash apply stash@{stash_number}

# Drops any stash by its number
$ git stash drop stash@{0}

# Apply the stash and then immediately drop it from your stack
$ git stash pop

# 'Release' a particular stash from your list of stashes
$ git stash pop stash@{stash_number}

# List all stashes
$ git stash list

# Show the latest stash changes
$ git stash show

# See diff details of a given stash number
$ git diff stash@{0}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Stash local changes</span>
$ git stash

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Stash local changes with a custom message</span>
$ git stash save <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>this is your custom message<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Re-apply the changes you saved in your latest stash</span>
$ git stash apply

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Re-apply the changes you saved in a given stash number</span>
$ git stash apply stash@{stash_number}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Drops any stash by its number</span>
$ git stash drop stash@{0}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Apply the stash and then immediately drop it from your stack</span>
$ git stash pop

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Release' a particular stash from your list of stashes</span>
$ git stash pop stash@{stash_number}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List all stashes</span>
$ git stash list

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show the latest stash changes</span>
$ git stash show

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> See diff details of a given stash number</span>
$ git diff stash@{0}</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-committing-files" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#committing-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Committing files</h4>
<p dir="auto">After adding/staging a file, the next step is to commit staged file(s)</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Commit staged file(s)
$ git commit -m 'commit message'

# Add file and commit
$ git commit filename -m 'commit message'

# Add file and commit staged file
$ git commit -am 'insert commit message'

# Amending a commit
$ git commit --amend 'new commit message' or no message to maintain previous message

# Squashing commits together
$ git rebase -i
This will give you an interface on your core editor:
# Commands:
#  p, pick = use commit
#  r, reword = use commit, but edit the commit message
#  e, edit = use commit, but stop for amending
#  s, squash = use commit, but meld into previous commit
#  f, fixup = like &quot;squash&quot;, but discard this commit's log message
#  x, exec = run command (the rest of the line) using shell

# Squashing commits together using reset --soft
$ git reset --soft HEAD~number_of_commits
$ git commit
** WARNING: this will require force pushing commits, which is OK if this is on a branch before you push to master or create a Pull Request."><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Commit staged file(s)</span>
$ git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>commit message<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Add file and commit</span>
$ git commit filename -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>commit message<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Add file and commit staged file</span>
$ git commit -am <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>insert commit message<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Amending a commit</span>
$ git commit --amend <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>new commit message<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> or no message to maintain previous message

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Squashing commits together</span>
$ git rebase -i
This will give you an interface on your core editor:
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Commands:</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  p, pick = use commit</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  r, reword = use commit, but edit the commit message</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  e, edit = use commit, but stop for amending</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  s, squash = use commit, but meld into previous commit</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  f, fixup = like "squash", but discard this commit's log message</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>  x, exec = run command (the rest of the line) using shell</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Squashing commits together using reset --soft</span>
$ git reset --soft HEAD~number_of_commits
$ git commit
<span class="pl-k">**</span> WARNING: this will require force pushing commits, which is OK <span class="pl-k">if</span> this is on a branch before you push to master or create a Pull Request.</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-branching-and-merging" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#branching-and-merging"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Branching and merging</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Creating a local branch
$ git checkout -b branchname

# Switching between 2 branches (in fact, this would work on terminal as well to switch between 2 directories - $ cd -)
$ git checkout -

# Pushing local branch to remote
$ git push -u origin branchname

# Deleting a local branch - this won't let you delete a branch that hasn't been merged yet
$ git branch -d branchname

# Deleting a local branch - this WILL delete a branch even if it hasn't been merged yet!
$ git branch -D branchname

# Remove any remote refs you have locally that have been removed from your remote (you can substitute &lt;origin&gt; to any remote branch)
$ git remote prune origin

# Viewing all branches, including local and remote branches
$ git branch -a

# Viewing all branches that have been merged into your current branch, including local and remote
$ git branch -a --merged

# Viewing all branches that haven't been merged into your current branch, including local and remote
$ git branch -a --no-merged

# Viewing local branches
$ git branch

# Viewing remote branches
$ git branch -r

# Rebase master branch into local branch
$ git rebase origin/master

# Pushing local branch after rebasing master into local branch
$ git push origin +branchname"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Creating a local branch</span>
$ git checkout -b branchname

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Switching between 2 branches (in fact, this would work on terminal as well to switch between 2 directories - $ cd -)</span>
$ git checkout -

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Pushing local branch to remote</span>
$ git push -u origin branchname

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Deleting a local branch - this won't let you delete a branch that hasn't been merged yet</span>
$ git branch -d branchname

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Deleting a local branch - this WILL delete a branch even if it hasn't been merged yet!</span>
$ git branch -D branchname

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Remove any remote refs you have locally that have been removed from your remote (you can substitute &lt;origin&gt; to any remote branch)</span>
$ git remote prune origin

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Viewing all branches, including local and remote branches</span>
$ git branch -a

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Viewing all branches that have been merged into your current branch, including local and remote</span>
$ git branch -a --merged

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Viewing all branches that haven't been merged into your current branch, including local and remote</span>
$ git branch -a --no-merged

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Viewing local branches</span>
$ git branch

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Viewing remote branches</span>
$ git branch -r

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Rebase master branch into local branch</span>
$ git rebase origin/master

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Pushing local branch after rebasing master into local branch</span>
$ git push origin +branchname</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-fetching-and-checking-out-remote-branches" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#fetching-and-checking-out-remote-branches"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Fetching and checking out remote branches</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# This will fetch all the remote branches for you.
$ git fetch origin

# With the remote branches in hand, you now need to check out the branch you are interested in, giving you a local working copy:
$ git checkout -b test origin/test

# Deleting a remote branch
$ git branch -rd origin/branchname
$ git push origin --delete branchname  or  $ git push origin:branchname"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> This will fetch all the remote branches for you.</span>
$ git fetch origin

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> With the remote branches in hand, you now need to check out the branch you are interested in, giving you a local working copy:</span>
$ git checkout -b <span class="pl-c1">test</span> origin/test

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Deleting a remote branch</span>
$ git branch -rd origin/branchname
$ git push origin --delete branchname  or  $ git push origin:branchname</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-merging-branch-to-trunkmaster" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#merging-branch-to-trunkmaster"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Merging branch to trunk/master</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# First checkout trunk/master
$ git checkout trunk/master

# Now merge branch to trunk/master
$ git merge branchname

# To cancel a merge
$ git merge --abort"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> First checkout trunk/master</span>
$ git checkout trunk/master

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Now merge branch to trunk/master</span>
$ git merge branchname

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> To cancel a merge</span>
$ git merge --abort</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-updating-a-local-repository-with-changes-from-a-github-repository" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#updating-a-local-repository-with-changes-from-a-github-repository"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Updating a local repository with changes from a Github repository</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git pull origin master"><pre>$ git pull origin master</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-tracking-existing-branch" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#tracking-existing-branch"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Tracking existing branch</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git branch --set-upstream-to=origin/foo foo"><pre>$ git branch --set-upstream-to=origin/foo foo</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-resetting" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#resetting"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Resetting</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Mixes your head with a give sha
# This lets you do things like split a commit
$ git reset --mixed [sha]

# Upstream master
$ git reset HEAD origin/master -- filename

# The version from the most recent commit
$ git reset HEAD -- filename

# The version before the most recent commit
$ git reset HEAD^ -- filename

# Move head to specific commit
$ git reset --hard sha

# Reset the staging area and the working directory to match the most recent commit. In addition to unstaging changes, the --hard flag tells Git to overwrite all changes in the working directory, too.
$ git reset --hard"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Mixes your head with a give sha</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> This lets you do things like split a commit</span>
$ git reset --mixed [sha]

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Upstream master</span>
$ git reset HEAD origin/master -- filename

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> The version from the most recent commit</span>
$ git reset HEAD -- filename

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> The version before the most recent commit</span>
$ git reset HEAD^ -- filename

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Move head to specific commit</span>
$ git reset --hard sha

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Reset the staging area and the working directory to match the most recent commit. In addition to unstaging changes, the --hard flag tells Git to overwrite all changes in the working directory, too.</span>
$ git reset --hard</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-git-remote" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#git-remote"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Git remote</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Show where 'origin' is pointing to and also tracked branches
$ git remote show origin

# Show where 'origin' is pointing to
$ git remote -v

# Change the 'origin' remote's URL
$ git remote set-url origin https://github.com/user/repo.git

# Add a new 'origin'
# Usually use to 'rebase' from forks
$ git remote add [NAME] https://github.com/user/fork-repo.git"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show where 'origin' is pointing to and also tracked branches</span>
$ git remote show origin

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show where 'origin' is pointing to</span>
$ git remote -v

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Change the 'origin' remote's URL</span>
$ git remote set-url origin https://github.com/user/repo.git

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Add a new 'origin'</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Usually use to 'rebase' from forks</span>
$ git remote add [NAME] https://github.com/user/fork-repo.git</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-git-grep" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#git-grep"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Git grep</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# 'Searches' for parts of strings in a directory
$ git grep 'something'

# 'Searches' for parts of strings in a directory and the -n prints out the line numbers where git has found matches
$ git grep -n 'something'

# 'Searches' for parts of string in a context (some lines before and some after the grepped term)
$ git grep -C&lt;number of lines&gt; 'something'

# 'Searches' for parts of string and also shows lines BEFORE the grepped term
$ git grep -B&lt;number of lines&gt; 'something'

# 'Searches' for parts of string and also shows lines AFTER the grepped term
$ git grep -A&lt;number of lines&gt; 'something'"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Searches' for parts of strings in a directory</span>
$ git grep <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Searches' for parts of strings in a directory and the -n prints out the line numbers where git has found matches</span>
$ git grep -n <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Searches' for parts of string in a context (some lines before and some after the grepped term)</span>
$ git grep -C<span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>number of lines<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Searches' for parts of string and also shows lines BEFORE the grepped term</span>
$ git grep -B<span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>number of lines<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> 'Searches' for parts of string and also shows lines AFTER the grepped term</span>
$ git grep -A<span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>number of lines<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span></pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-git-blame" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#git-blame"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Git blame</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Show alteration history of a file with the name of the author
$ git blame [filename]

# Show alteration history of a file with the name of the author &amp;&amp; SHA
$ git blame [filename] -l"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show alteration history of a file with the name of the author</span>
$ git blame [filename]

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show alteration history of a file with the name of the author &amp;&amp; SHA</span>
$ git blame [filename] -l</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-git-log" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#git-log"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Git log</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Show a list of all commits in a repository. This command shows everything about a commit, such as commit ID, author, date and commit message.
$ git log

# List of commits showing commit messages and changes
$ git log -p

# List of commits with the particular expression you are looking for
$ git log -S 'something'

# List of commits by author
$ git log --author 'Author Name'

# Show a list of commits in a repository in a more summarised way. This shows a shorter version of the commit ID and the commit message.
$ git log --oneline

# Show a list of commits in a repository since yesterday
$ git log --since=yesterday

# Shows log by author and searching for specific term inside the commit message
$ git log --grep &quot;term&quot; --author &quot;name&quot;"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show a list of all commits in a repository. This command shows everything about a commit, such as commit ID, author, date and commit message.</span>
$ git log

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List of commits showing commit messages and changes</span>
$ git log -p

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List of commits with the particular expression you are looking for</span>
$ git log -S <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>something<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List of commits by author</span>
$ git log --author <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Author Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show a list of commits in a repository in a more summarised way. This shows a shorter version of the commit ID and the commit message.</span>
$ git log --oneline

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show a list of commits in a repository since yesterday</span>
$ git log --since=yesterday

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Shows log by author and searching for specific term inside the commit message</span>
$ git log --grep <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>term<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> --author <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>name<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-checking-what-you-are-committing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#checking-what-you-are-committing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Checking what you are committing</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# See all (non-staged) changes done to a local repo
$ git diff

# See all (staged) changes done to a local repo
$ git diff --cached

# Check what the changes between the files you've committed and the live repo
$ git diff --stat origin/master"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> See all (non-staged) changes done to a local repo</span>
$ git diff

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> See all (staged) changes done to a local repo</span>
$ git diff --cached

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Check what the changes between the files you've committed and the live repo</span>
$ git diff --stat origin/master</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-useful-commands" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#useful-commands"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Useful commands</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Check if a sha is in production
$ git tag --contains [sha]

# Number of commits by author
$ git shortlog -s --author 'Author Name'

# List of authors and commits to a repository sorted alphabetically
$ git shortlog -s -n

# List of commit comments by author
$ git shortlog -n --author 'Author Name'
# This also shows the total number of commits by the author

# Number of commits by contributors
$ git shortlog -s -n

# Undo local changes to a File
$ git checkout -- filename

# Shows more detailed info about a commit
$ git cat-file sha -p

# Show number of lines added and removed from a repository by an author since some time in the past.
$ git log --author=&quot;Author name&quot; --pretty=tformat: --numstat --since=month | awk '{ add += $1; subs += $2; loc += $1 - $2 } END { printf &quot;added lines: %s, removed lines: %s, total lines: %s\n&quot;, add, subs, loc }'"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Check if a sha is in production</span>
$ git tag --contains [sha]

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Number of commits by author</span>
$ git shortlog -s --author <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Author Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List of authors and commits to a repository sorted alphabetically</span>
$ git shortlog -s -n

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> List of commit comments by author</span>
$ git shortlog -n --author <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Author Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> This also shows the total number of commits by the author</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Number of commits by contributors</span>
$ git shortlog -s -n

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Undo local changes to a File</span>
$ git checkout -- filename

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Shows more detailed info about a commit</span>
$ git cat-file sha -p

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Show number of lines added and removed from a repository by an author since some time in the past.</span>
$ git log --author=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Author name<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> --pretty=tformat: --numstat --since=month <span class="pl-k">|</span> awk <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>{ add += $1; subs += $2; loc += $1 - $2 } END { printf "added lines: %s, removed lines: %s, total lines: %s\n", add, subs, loc }<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span></pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-useful-alias" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#useful-alias"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Useful alias</h4>
<p dir="auto">To add an alias simply open your .gitconfig file on your home directory and include the alias code</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Shows the log in a more consisted way with the graph for branching and merging
lg = log --color --graph --pretty=format:'%Cred%h%Creset -%C(yellow)%d%Creset %s %Cgreen(%cr) %C(bold blue)&lt;%an&gt;%Creset' --abbrev-commit"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Shows the log in a more consisted way with the graph for branching and merging</span>
lg = log --color --graph --pretty=format:<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>%Cred%h%Creset -%C(yellow)%d%Creset %s %Cgreen(%cr) %C(bold blue)&lt;%an&gt;%Creset<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> --abbrev-commit</pre></div>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-contributing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#contributing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Contributing</h3>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Fork it!</li>
<li>Create your feature branch: <code>git checkout -b my-new-feature</code></li>
<li>Commit your changes: <code>git commit -m 'Add some feature'</code></li>
<li>Push to the branch: <code>git push -u origin my-new-feature</code></li>
<li>Submit a pull request - cheers!</li>
</ol>
</article>
  </div>

    </div>

  </readme-toc>
